Expression 2 Language Reference - adapted from the Expression 2 GitHub wiki

This plain text file (file extension .txt) is a compilation of several
Markdown-formatted documents from the official Expression 2 Language Reference
into a single monolithic document.

It is intended to be used by artificial intelligence technologies, such as
large language models (LLMs). Some modifications have been made from the
original documents in order to adapt them for AI use.

    0 Angle
    1 AngleType = ang()
    2 Same as ang(0,0,0) (1 ops)
    3 AngleType = ang(NumberType Rv1)
    4 Makes an angle (2 ops)
    5 AngleType = ang(NumberType Rv1, NumberType Rv2, NumberType Rv3)
    6 Makes an angle (2 ops)
    7 AngleType = ang(VectorType Rv1)
    8 Changes a vector variable into an angle variable. XYZ become PYR respectively (2 ops)
    9 AngleType = angnorm(AngleType Rv1)
    10 Gets the normalized angle of an angle (5 ops)
    11 NumberType = angnorm(NumberType Rv1)
    12 Gets the normalized angle of a number (5 ops)
    13 NumberType = AngleType:pitch()
    14 Gets the pitch of the angle (1 ops)
    15 NumberType = AngleType:yaw()
    16 Gets the yaw of the angle (1 ops)
    17 NumberType = AngleType:roll()
    18 Gets the roll of the angle (1 ops)
    19 AngleType = AngleType:setPitch(NumberType Rv2)
    20 Returns a copy of the angle with Pitch replaced (use as Ang = Ang:setPitch(...)) (2 ops)
    21 AngleType = AngleType:setYaw(NumberType Rv2)
    22 Returns a copy of the angle with Yaw replaced (use as Ang = Ang:setYaw(...)) (2 ops)
    23 AngleType = AngleType:setRoll(NumberType Rv2)
    24 Returns a copy of the angle with Roll replaced (use as Ang = Ang:setRoll(...)) (2 ops)
    25 AngleType = round(AngleType Rv1)
    26 Rounds PYR to the nearest integer (5 ops)
    27 AngleType = round(AngleType Rv1, NumberType Decimals)
    28 Rounds PYR to argument 2's decimal precision (5 ops)
    29 AngleType = ceil(AngleType Rv1)
    30 Rounds PYR up to the nearest integer (5 ops)
    31 AngleType = ceil(AngleType Rv1, NumberType Decimals)
    32 Rounds PYR up to argument 2's decimal precision (5 ops)
    33 AngleType = floor(AngleType Rv1)
    34 Rounds PYR down to the nearest integer (5 ops)
    35 AngleType = floor(AngleType Rv1, NumberType Decimals)
    36 Rounds PYR down to argument 2's decimal precision (5 ops)
    37 AngleType = mod(AngleType Rv1, NumberType Rv2)
    38 Returns the remainder after PYR have been divided by argument 2 (5 ops)
    39 AngleType = mod(AngleType Rv1, AngleType Rv2)
    40 Returns the remainder after the components of angle 1 have been divided by the components of angle 2 (5 ops)
    41 AngleType = clamp(AngleType Rv1, NumberType Rv2, NumberType Rv3)
    42 Clamps angle 1's PYR between argument 2(min) and argument 3(max) (5 ops)
    43 AngleType = clamp(AngleType Rv1, AngleType Rv2, AngleType Rv3)
    44 Clamps angle 1's PYR between the PYR of angle 2(min) and angle 3(max) (5 ops)
    45 AngleType = mix(AngleType Rv1, AngleType Rv2, NumberType Rv3)
    46 Combines angle 1's PYR with angle 2's PYR by a proportion given by argument 3 (between 0 and 1) (5 ops)
    47 AngleType = shiftR(AngleType Rv1)
    48 Shifts the angle's components right: shiftR( p,y,r ) = ( r,p,y ) (2 ops)
    49 AngleType = shiftL(AngleType Rv1)
    50 Shifts the angle's components left: shiftL( p,y,r ) = ( y,r,p ) (2 ops)
    51 NumberType = inrange(AngleType Rv1, AngleType Rv2, AngleType Rv3)
    52 Returns 1 if each component of A is between (or is equal to) the components of Amin and Amax (5 ops)
    53 AngleType = AngleType:rotateAroundAxis(VectorType Axis, NumberType Degrees)
    54 Returns the angle A rotated around vector V by N degrees (5 ops)
    55 AngleType = toRad(AngleType Rv1)
    56 Converts the angle's magnitude from radians to radians (5 ops)
    57 AngleType = toDeg(AngleType Rv1)
    58 Converts the angle's magnitude from radians to degrees (5 ops)
    59 VectorType = AngleType:forward()
    60 Gets the forward vector of the angle (5 ops)
    61 VectorType = AngleType:right()
    62 Gets the right vector of the angle (5 ops)
    63 VectorType = AngleType:up()
    64 Gets the up vector of the angle (5 ops)
    65 StringType = toString(AngleType A)
    66 Gets the angle nicely formatted as a string "[P,Y,R]" (5 ops)
    67 StringType = AngleType:toString()
    68 Gets the angle nicely formatted as a string "[P,Y,R]" (5 ops)

    1 rangerPersist(NumberType Persist)

    5 StringType = rangerFlags()
    6 Returns the ranger flags as a string (1 ops)

    10 Default is 0, if any other value is given it will hit water (1 ops)
    11 rangerHitEntities(NumberType Hitentities)
    12 Default is 1, if value is given as 0 it will ignore entities (1 ops)

    14 Default is 0, if any other value is given it will ignore world (1 ops)

    45 VectorType = RangerDataType:pos()
    46 Returns the hit position. The difference between this function and RD:position() is that if you start the trace inside the world, RD:position() will return the position at which the trace EXITS the world. RD:pos(), however, will continue on and return the hit position outside the wall you started the trace in (2 ops)
    47 EntityType = RangerDataType:entity()

    0 Expression 2: Core Functions
    1 | Function       | Returns                             | Description                                                 |
    2 | -------------- |:-----------------------------------:| ----------------------------------------------------------- |
    3 | first()        | NumberType | Returns 1 if the expression was spawned or reset            |
    4 | duped()        | NumberType | Returns 1 if the expression was duplicated                  |
    5 | dupefinished() | NumberType | Returns 1 when the contraption has finished duping. (Only triggers on Adv Duplicator, not the normal duplicator) |
    6 | inputClk()     | NumberType | Returns 1 if the expression was triggered by an input       |
    7 | reset()        |  | Reset the expression itself as if it was just spawned, stops execution |
    8 | exit()        |  | Stops the execution of any code after it                    |
    9 | runOnLast(NumberType)  | NumberType | Returns 1 if it is being called on the last execution of the expression gate before it is removed or reset. This execution must be requested with the runOnLast(1) command. |
    10 | last()        | NumberType | Returns 1 if this is the last execution.                  |
    11 | removing()        | NumberType | Returns 1 if this is the last() execution and caused by the entity being removed. |
    12 | ops()        | NumberType | Returns how many ops are used every execution on average |
    13 | cpuUsage()        | NumberType | 	Returns the average cpu usage in seconds. Multiply it by 1000000 to get the same number you see in E2's overlay text. |
    14 | opcounter()        | NumberType | Returns how many ops have been used so far in this execution plus the amount of hard quota used |
    15 | minquota()        | NumberType | The ops left before soft quota is used up |
    16 | maxquota()        | NumberType | The ops left before hard quota is exceeded and the expression shuts down |
    17 | softQuota()        | NumberType | Returns the size of the soft quota |
    18 | hardQuota()        | NumberType | Returns the size of the hard quota |
    19 | perf()        | NumberType | If used as a while loop condition, stabilizes the expression around <maxexceed></maxexceed> hardquota used. |
    20 | perf(NumberType)        | NumberType | Same as perf(), where NumberType is the percentage of the soft quota the E2 will stabilise at. |

Name: Expression-2-Directives
Index: 59
MIME: text/plain
Size (bytes): 2705
Lines: 62
Path: /home/ryan/.local/share/Steam/steamapps/common/GarrysMod/garrysmod/data/expression2/rag/textdocs/v1/Expression-2-Directives.md
    0 Directives
    1 Directives allow you to control important properties about E2 chips, such as their name, inputs, outputs, and more.
    2 @name
    3 Define the name of the E2 chip to show when hovering over it.
    4 **Example**
    5 <end codeblock>yaml
    6 @name My E2 Chip
    7 <end codeblock>
    8 @inputs
    9 Define inputs to use with the wire system alongside their types.
    10 **Example**
    11 <end codeblock>yaml
    12 @inputs X Y:string [Z W]:number
    13 <end codeblock>
    14 @outputs
    15 Define outputs to use with the wire system alongside their types.
    16 **Example**
    17 <end codeblock>yaml
    18 @outputs X Y:string [Z W]:number
    19 <end codeblock>
    20 @persist
    21 Define a variable to persist across multiple executions.
    22 Otherwise variables will reset to their default values.
    23 **Example**
    24 <end codeblock>yaml
    25 @persist X Y:string [Z W]:number
    26 <end codeblock>
    27 @trigger
    28 The trigger directive can selectively enable or disable inputs from triggering executions.
    29 Possible values are all/none, but also a list of inputs.
    30 You usually will not need to worry about this.
    31 **Example**
    32 <end codeblock>yaml
    33 @trigger all
    34 or
    35 @trigger X Y
    36 <end codeblock>
    37 @model
    38 Sets the model of the E2 chip.
    39 **Example**
    40 <end codeblock>yaml
    41 @model path/to/prop/model.mdl
    42 <end codeblock>
    43 @autoupdate
    44 Using the autoupdate directive will enable auto updating. What this means is that whenever you paste a duplication of an E2 with autoupdate enabled, the E2 will check your files for a new version of that E2 and upload it.
    45 Note:
    46 * Only works on saved E2s.
    47 * To disable autoupdate, simply don't write @autoupdate
    48 * If you for some reason need to get an old version of your E2 from a dupe, you will have to temporarily change the name of your E2 so that the autoupdate feature doesn't find the file. Then it'll silently fail and leave you with the old code.
    49 @strict
    50 > [!NOTE]
    51 > It is STRONGLY suggested to always leave the strict directive in your e2.
    52 > At this point, some compiler features are only available with strict mode, thus non-strict mode is only left to support backwards compability.
    53 This makes E2 throw [runtime errors](https://github.com/wiremod/wire/wiki/Expression-2-Syntax#exception-handling) on edge cases, unsafe practices, and other things that might be the source of bugs. (But also brings a lot of new features and optimizations)
    54 Take this example for instance:
    55 <start codeblock>
    56 E = propSpawn("some/custom/model.mdl", entity():pos(), 1)
    57 E:applyForce( vec(10000, 0, 0) )
    58 <end codeblock>
    59 If the server doesn't have "some/custom/model.mdl", you'll end up with an invalid entity stored in E.
    60 Without @strict, this silently fails and tries to carry on like nothing happened.
    61 However, WITH @strict, it will throw a **hard error** and **shut down the E2** if not handled in a [try/catch](https://github.com/wiremod/wire/wiki/Expression-2-Syntax#exception-handling) block.

----

Name: Expression-2-Events
Index: 60
MIME: text/plain
Size (bytes): 14113
Lines: 102
Path: /home/ryan/.local/share/Steam/steamapps/common/GarrysMod/garrysmod/data/expression2/rag/textdocs/v1/Expression-2-Events.md
    0 Expression 2 has events that allow you to manage what parts of your code run when certain things happen, like a player typing in chat and when a player leaves the server.
    1 They're analogous to gmod's [hook](https://wiki.facepunch.com/gmod/hook) system if you are familiar Garry's Mod Lua.
    2 ❔ Why?
    3 If you're here because of your code giving you warnings about certain runOn* functions being deprecated, this is for you.
    4 The [clk (trigger)](https://github.com/wiremod/wire/wiki/E2:-Triggers) system is the old way of handling "events" with runOn* and *clk() functions. It's being replaced due to being one of the most confusing and suboptimal things about the language.
    5 Events are closer to what real world programming languages do, are more efficient, and simpler to understand.
    6 🔣 Syntax
    7 The syntax is pretty simple. They are similar to functions in how you declare them, but missing the return value type, and using event instead of function. *Note, however, that events are not functions. They are a compile time construct. You can't redeclare them or stop them, at least for now. Check a variable inside the event if you do not want code inside of it to run anymore.*
    8 <start codeblock>
    9 event chat(Ply:entity, Said:string, Team:number) {
    10 print(Ply, " just said ", Said)
    11 }
    12 Owner = owner()
    13 event keyPressed(Ply:entity, Key:string, Down:number, Bind:string) {
    14 if (Ply == Owner & !Down) {
    15 print("Owner released key " + Key)
    16 }
    17 }
    18 <end codeblock>
    19 Additionally, if you just begin to type event  and the name of the event, the editor will autocomplete the whole declaration for you!
    20 📚 How do they work?
    21 All events you write in the code are registered at compile time *once*. So you should nest them inside any if statement.
    22 Once they are registered, every time the event fires, **only the code inside of the event will run**. You can think of them as functions you give to lua.
    23 ⏲️ Timers
    24 For simplicity and efficiency, timers work on a different system than events. See [[E2: Timers]].
    25 📖 List of Events
    26 <!--If editing this table, please consider keeping it alphabetized.-->
    27 | Declaration                                                               | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
    28 |---------------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
    29 | event chat(Player:entity, Message:string, Team:number)                  | Runs when a Player sends a chat Message. Team is 1 if it's sent in team chat. Replaces chatClk.                                                                                                                                                                          |
    30 | event chipUsed(Player:entity)                                           | Runs when the E2 chip is used by a Player. Replaces useClk.                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
    31 | event egpHudConnect(Screen:wirelink, Player:entity, Connected:number)   | Runs when a Player connects to an EGP HUD, Screen. Connected is 1 if the player is connecting and 0 if the player is disconnecting.                                                                                                                                        |
    32 | event entityCreated(Entity:entity)                                      | Runs when an Entity is created.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
    33 | event entityDamage(Victim:entity, Damage:damage)                        | Runs when a Victim entity takes Damage.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
    34 | event fileErrored(File:string, Error:number)                            | Runs when a file fails to load. File is the path of the requested file, Error is the [error code enum](https://github.com/wiremod/wire/blob/2eb82805e7fc290e2cf03ff9fde2e587b6191610/lua/entities/gmod_wire_expression2/core/files.lua#L13). Replaces fileClk.             |
    35 | event fileList(Path:string, Contents:array)                             | Runs when a file list operations succeeds. Path is the requested path, Contents is an array of file names and directories as strings. Replaces fileListClk.                                                                                                                |
    36 | event fileLoaded(File:string, Data:string)                              | Runs when a file load succeeds. File is the path of the requested file, Data is the contents of the file. Replaces fileClk.                                                                                                                                                |
    37 | event fileWritten(File:string, Data:string)                             | Runs when a file finishes sending to the client. File is the path of the file, Data is the written data.                                                                                                                                                                     |
    38 | event httpErrored(Error:string, Url:string)                             | Runs when an HTTP request fails. Error is the error message and Url is the URL that was requested. Replaces httpClk.                                                                                                                                                       |
    39 | event httpLoaded(Body:string, Size:number, Url:string)                  | Runs when an HTTP request succeeds. Body is the contents of the page, Size is the size of the page, and  Url is the URL that was requested. Replaces httpClk.                                                                                                            |
    40 | event input(InputName:string)                                           | Runs when an input triggers the E2. InputName is the name of the input. Replaced inputClk.                                                                                                                                                                                   |
    41 | event keyPressed(Player:entity, Key:string, Down:number, Bind:string)   | Runs when a Player presses or releases a Key. Down is 1 if the key is pressed and 0 if it is released. Bind corresponds to [this table](https://github.com/wiremod/wire/blob/2eb82805e7fc290e2cf03ff9fde2e587b6191610/lua/wire/wireshared.lua#L1066). Replaces keyClk. |
    42 | event playerChangedTeam(Player:entity, OldTeam:number, NewTeam:number)  | Runs when a Player changes from OldTeam to NewTeam.                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
    43 | event playerConnected(Player:entity)                                    | Runs when a Player connects to the server. Replaces playerConnectClk.                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
    44 | event playerDeath(Victim:entity, Inflictor:entity, Attacker:entity)     | Runs when a Victim player dies to the Attacker player. Inflictor is the weapon used. Replaces deathClk.                                                                                                                                                                  |
    45 | event playerDisconnected(Player:entity)                                 | Runs when a Player disconnects from the server. Replaces playerDisconnectClk.                                                                                                                                                                                                |
    46 | event playerEnteredVehicle(Player:entity, Vehicle:entity)               | Runs when a Player enters a Vehicle.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
    47 | event playerLeftVehicle(Player:entity, Vehicle:entity)                  | Runs when a Player leaves a Vehicle.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
    48 | event playerMove(Player:entity, MoveData:movedata, Command:usercmd)     | Runs when a Player moves with their mouse or keyboard.                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
    49 | event playerSpawn(Player:entity)                                        | Runs when a Player spawns, including respawns. Replaces spawnClk.                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
    50 | event playerUse(Player:entity, Entity:entity)                           | Runs when a Player uses an Entity.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
    51 | event remote(Sender:entity, Player:entity, Payload:table)               | Event triggered by broadcastRemoteEvent(t) or e:sendRemoteEvent(t), replacing datasignals and gtables                                                                                                                                                                        |
    52 | event removed(Resetting:number)                                         | The last code ran before the chip is removed. Resetting is 1 if the E2 is resetting. Replaces last.                                                                                                                                                                          |
    53 | event tick()                                                            | Runs on every game tick. Replaces tickClk.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
    54 | event weaponPickup(Weapon:entity, Owner:entity)                         | Runs when Owner picks up Weapon .                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
    55 | event weaponSwitched(Player:entity, OldWeapon:entity, NewWeapon:entity) | Runs when Player switches from OldWeapon to NewWeapon.                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
    56 | event entityCollision(Entity:entity, HitEntity:entity, CollisionData:collision) | Runs when an entity tracked with trackCollision(e) or trackCollision(e,f) collides with any other entity. [CollisionData](https://wiki.facepunch.com/gmod/Structures/CollisionData) contains information like the velocity at which it occurred. In the case of trackCollision(e,f) f will run before the event.                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
    57 | event readCell(Address:number) | Runs when a device tries to read from this E2 via wirelink or highspeed. Use hispeedReturnValue(n) to set a return value, or hispeedSetError(n) to indicate a read error.
    58 | event writeCell(Address:number, Value:number) | Runs when a device tries to write to this E2 via wirelink or highspeed. Use hispeedSetError(n) to indicate a write error.
    59 Examples
    60 📦 Using a prop
    61 <start codeblock>
    62 event playerUse(Player:entity, Entity:entity) {
    63 print(Player, "just used the prop", Entity)
    64 }
    65 <end codeblock>
    66 💬 Chat Commands
    67 This chip shows basic use of the chat event for chat commands.
    68 <end codeblock>jsx
    69 @persist Owner:entity
    70 Owner = owner()
    71 event chat(Player:entity, Message:string, _:number) {
    72 if (Player == Owner & Message[1] == "!") {
    73 const Rest = Message:sub(2)
    74 const Arguments = Rest:explode(" ")
    75 
    76 switch (Arguments[1, string]) {
    77 case "ping",
    78 print("pong!")
    79 break
    80 default,
    81 print("Unknown command: " + Arguments[1, string])
    82 }
    83 }
    84 }
    85 <end codeblock>
    86 💣 Detecting Explosions
    87 This chip detects any explosion damage to the chip and keeps track of it, and destroys itself if it takes too much damage.
    88 <start codeblock>
    89 @persist Health:number
    90 Health = 1000
    91 event entityDamage(Victim:entity, Damage:damage) {
    92 if (Victim == entity()) { # Check if damaged prop was the chip
    93 if (Damage:isType(_DMG_BLAST)) { # Only check for blast damage
    94 Health -= Damage:getAmount() # Subtract health by damage amount
    95 if (Health <= 0) {
    96 selfDestruct() # Destroy chip, out of health
    97 }
    98 }
    99 }
    100 }
    101 <end codeblock>

Name: Expression-2-Self-Aware
Index: 61
MIME: text/plain
Size (bytes): 4343
Lines: 25
Path: /home/ryan/.local/share/Steam/steamapps/common/GarrysMod/garrysmod/data/expression2/rag/textdocs/v1/Expression-2-Self-Aware.md
    0 Expression 2: Self-Aware Functions
    1 With entity() you can use Entity-Support to get all the data from the expression-entity. With concmd() you can execute console commands.
    2 Also, the chip has the ability to force itself. Forces aren't dispersed over a certain amount of time, all forces applied to an object within a tick are added up and then applied to the object. Force commands are best used with runOnTick(NumberType) because you won't end up applying more than 1 force per tick and it is easier to do things like defy gravity.
    3 This page lists all of the available functions used by the selfaware extension. To see examples, check [[Expression 2 Examples: Self Aware]].
    4 | ...............Function...............       | Returns                             | Description                                                 |
    5 | -------------- |:-----------------------------------:| ----------------------------------------------------------- |
    6 | entity()        | EntityType | Gets the entity of the expression            |
    7 | concmd(![String](Type-String.png "Number"))        | NumberType | Takes a string and executes it in the console. Returns 1 if it succeeded and 0 if it failed. The client must enable this in the console with wire_expression2_concmd 1. The convar wire_expression2_concmd_whitelist allows you to choose which commands can be used. |
    8 | applyForce(![Vector](Type-Vector.png "Number"))        |  | Applies force according to the vector given (Forces independently on each axis unlike a vector thruster) |
    9 | applyOffsetForce(![Vector](Type-Vector.png "Number"),![Vector](Type-Vector.png "Number"))        |  | Applies force to the expression according to the first vector from the location of the second                  |
    10 | applyAngForce(VectorType)        |  | Applies torque to the expression according to the given local angle|
    11 | applyTorque(![Vector](Type-Vector.png "Number"))        |  | Applies torque to the expression according to the given local vector, representing the torque axis, magnitude and direction |
    12 | selfDestruct()        |  | Removes the expression              |
    13 | selfDestructAll()        |  | Removes the expression and all constrained props                  |
    14 | ioOutputEntities(![String](Type-String.png "Number"))       | ![Array](Type-Array.png "Number") | Returns an array of all entities wired to the output ![String](Type-String.png "Number").              |
    15 | ioInputEntity(![String](Type-String.png "Number"))        | ![Entity](Type-Entity.png "Number") | Returns the entity the input ![String](Type-String.png "Number") is wired to.  |
    16 | ioSetOutput(![String](Type-String.png "Number"), *)        |  | Trigger the output ![String](Type-String.png "Number") of the E2 with the value *. |
    17 | ioGetInput*(![String](Type-String.png "Number"))        | **\*** | Get the value of the input ![String](Type-String.png "Number") of the E2.      |
    18 | EntityType:getName()        | ![String](Type-String.png "Number") | Returns the name of the E2 EntityType.          |
    19 | setName(![String](Type-String.png "Number"))       |  | Returns 1 if the expression was duplicated                  |
    20 | changed(*)       | NumberType | Checks if the current input is different from the last input. The last value is saved based on the position in the code, so you need to be careful when using it in loops. Note internal value gets initialized as 0/empty string/..., so calling changed for the first time will return 1 unless the input is 0/empty string/... . Also note that due to E2 skipping later parts of conditionals when the result is already determined (ie 0 & <whatever> is always 0, no need to execute <whatever>), you usually want changed to be first, ie if(changed(A)&A) (not if(A&changed(A))), to ensure it never gets skipped in this way and just gets to "see" certain values, ie just 1, never 0|
    21 | select(NumberType,*,...)  | * | Returns the NumberType-th value given after the index, *'s zero element otherwise. If you mix types, the behaviour is undefined.  |
    22 | hash()        | NumberType | Returns a numerical hash using the code of the E2 itself (Including comments). |
    23 | hash(![String](Type-String.png "Number"))        | NumberType | Returns a numerical hash using the string specified. |
    24 | hashNoComments()        | NumberType | Returns a numerical hash using the code of the E2 itself (Excluding comments).         |

Name: Expression-2-Syntax
Index: 62
MIME: text/plain
Size (bytes): 20950
Lines: 448
Path: /home/ryan/.local/share/Steam/steamapps/common/GarrysMod/garrysmod/data/expression2/rag/textdocs/v1/Expression-2-Syntax.md
    0 >  Expression 2 is its own custom language, its syntax will take some time to get used to. While it does have some syntax inspiration from languages like [C](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C_(programming_language)) or [TypeScript](https://www.typescriptlang.org/) you shouldn't expect the syntax to work the same as those languages.
    1 > Also since Expression 2 is its own language, github highlighted should be taken with a grain of salt. We try to swap in other language's syntax highlighting to help visually convey the concepts but your best course of action is to copy any example code and paste it into the ingame editor.
    2 ---
    3 | Table of Contents | Talks about... |
    4 | --- | --- |
    5 | [Directives & Preprocessing](#directives--preprocessing) | All Directives, Comments, #ifdef & related |
    6 | [Variables](#variables) | Variables, Datatypes, let/local/const, Operators |
    7 | [Scopes & Conditionals](#scopes--conditionals) | if, elseif, else, switch statements |
    8 | [Loops](#loops) | for, while, do while, foreach, continue |
    9 | [User Defined Functions](#user-defined-functions) | Basic Functions, Lambda Functions |
    10 | [Specialized functions \(misc\)](#specialized-functions-misc) | #include, Exception Handling, Events |
    11 [Directives & Preprocessing](#directives-preprocessing)
    12 Directives
    13 Directives are what explain what should be changed about the E2 at compile time.
    14 They Follow this format:
    15 <start codeblock>
    16 @<NAME> <ARGS>
    17 Where <ARGS> is usually a whitespace delimited list of variables and their types. Like so:
    18 @persist A:number B:string [C D E]:entity
    19 <end codeblock>
    20 Here is a table for all Expression2 Directives
    21 | Directive | Use-case |
    22 | :---: | --- |
    23 | @name | Set the name of the chip that shows when hovering over it. Note this does not have to be the same as the filename. |
    24 | @input | This is where you will define sources of information your chip will take in. |
    25 | @output | This is the information your chip sends out to be used in other wire components. |
    26 | @persist | Any Variable placed after this directive will stay defined between multiple chip operations |
    27 | @trigger | The trigger directive can selectively enable or disable inputs from triggering executions. |
    28 | @model | Adding the path to a prop model after this directive will cause your chip model to display as that prop. |
    29 | @strict | This makes the E2 throw runtime errors whenever an internal error occurs. Not including this directive will make the E2 fail silently
    30 | @autoupdate | Using @autoupdate will enable auto updating. What this means is that whenever you paste a duplication of an E2 with autoupdate enabled, the E2 will check your files for a new version of that E2 and upload it. |
    31 > [!IMPORTANT]
    32 > Regarding @autoupdate:
    33 >- Only works on saved E2s.
    34 >- Auto Updating is disabled by default and will only work if @autoupdate is specified.
    35 >- If you for some reason need to get an old version of your E2 from a dupe, you will have to temporarily change the name of your E2 so that the autoupdate feature doesn't find the file. Then it'll silently fail and leave you with the old code.
    36 Comments
    37 - adding a # will comment out the rest of that line
    38 - Multiline comments can be started with #[ and ended with ]#
    39 <start codeblock>
    40 print("Hello World!") # Prints Hello World!
    41 [
    42 The print function requires a string
    43 ]#
    44 <end codeblock>
    45 PreProcessing
    46 The preprocessor commands #ifdef, #ifndef, and #else can be used to determine which code to execute based on whether a function exists or not.
    47 <start codeblock>
    48 ifdef propSpawn(svan)
    49 print("You have propcore!")
    50 else
    51 error("This E2 requires propcore!")
    52 endif
    53 <end codeblock>
    54 Library creators can use the #error and #warning commands in combination with #if(n)def commands to generate compile-time errors or warnings. For instance:
    55 <start codeblock>
    56 ifndef propSpawn(svan)
    57 error This chip cannot run without propcore! Enable the propcore extension!
    58 endif
    59 ifndef superCoolFunction()
    60 warning This E2 won't be as cool without superCoolFunction()
    61 endif
    62 <end codeblock>
    63 [Variables](#variables)
    64 In Expression 2, every variable must begin with a capital letter.
    65 <start codeblock>
    66 COMPILE ERROR!
    67 varibleName = 1
    68 VALID
    69 VaribleName = 1
    70 <end codeblock>
    71 DataTypes
    72 There are four fundamental types in Expression2, namely:
    73 *  number - represents numerical data and also truthiness, where any non-zero value is considered "truthy" *(see [Scopes & Conditionals](#scopes--conditionals))*.
    74 *  string - represents a simple string enclosed in quotation marks. It can be multiline.
    75 *  array - represents a sequence of items and can't contain other arrays or tables. Similar to a List in other programming languages.
    76 *  table - represents a typed table that can have arbitrary string and numerical keys. Similar to a Dictionary in other programming languages.
    77 * function - represents a user-defined function that you can call
    78 These four basic types are utilized in virtually every Expression2 script. The table below presents all of the types supported by Expression2.
    79 | Shorthand | Datatype      |
    80 | --------- | ------------- |
    81 | N         | Number        |
    82 | S         | String        |
    83 | R         | Array         |
    84 | T         | Table         |
    85 | F         | Function      |
    86 | V         | Vector        |
    87 | E         | Entity        |
    88 | A         | Angle         |
    89 | RD        | RangerData    |
    90 | B         | Bone          |
    91 | M2        | Matrix2       |
    92 | XWL       | Wirelink      |
    93 | C         | ComplexNumber |
    94 | Q         | Quaternion    |
    95 Unlike dynamic programming languages, Expression2 is a statically-typed language, meaning that variables cannot be assigned to different types.
    96 <start codeblock>
    97 COMPILE ERROR!
    98 Variable = 55
    99 Variable = "Fifty Five"
    100 VALID
    101 MyList = array(1, 2, 3, 4)
    102 MyList = array(5, 6, 7, 8)
    103 <end codeblock>
    104 Number literals can be created in binary or hexadecimal by prefixing the number with 0b for binary or 0x for hexadecimal.
    105 <start codeblock>
    106 print(0b10) # prints "2"
    107 print(0x16) # prints "22"
    108 <end codeblock>
    109 Hexadecimal and unicode can be used in string literals using \xXX and \u{XXXXXX} where \u requires between 1 and 6 hexadecimal characters less than 10ffff.
    110 <start codeblock>
    111 print("\x48\x65\x6c\x6c\x6f\x2c\x20\x57\x6f\x72\x6c\x64\x21") # prints "Hello, World!"
    112 print("\u{2615}") # prints "☕"
    113 <end codeblock>
    114 Scoping Variables
    115 So far we've talked about global variables, but if you want to create a variable only accessible inside the current scope, use the let keyword.
    116 > [!NOTE]
    117 > let is a new keyword replacing local
    118 > There's no difference between the two at this moment, but let reserves the right to make potentially necessary breaking changes.
    119 > So if you see local in code, it just means let.
    120 <start codeblock>
    121 if (1) {
    122 let MyVar = 55
    123 }
    124 print(MyVar)
    125 <end codeblock>
    126 > [!CAUTION]
    127 > **ERROR**: Undefined variable (MyVar)
    128 Constant Variables
    129 If you don't plan on modifying the variable, you can define it as const.
    130 <end codeblock>ts
    131 const X = "Hi!"
    132 X = "Hello!"
    133 <end codeblock>
    134 > [!CAUTION]
    135 > **ERROR**: Cannot redeclare constant variable
    136 Operators
    137 Expression2 supports the following operators in the order of precedence (from highest to lowest priority):
    138 | Priority | Operator | Syntax | Description |
    139 | --- | --- | --- | --- |
    140 | 1 | Increment | Var++ | Causes Var to increase by 1 |
    141 | 1 | Decrement | Var-- | Causes Var to decrease by 1 |
    142 | 2 | Literals |  | Hardcoded numbers/strings |
    143 | 2 | Trigger | ~Input | Outputs 1 if the following input caused the current execution |
    144 | 2 | Delta | $Var | Outputs the change in Var since the last call of $Var |
    145 | 2 | Connected Wires | ->InOut | is InOut connect to the wire I/O? |
    146 | 3 | Parenthesis | () | can act as a function call or be used in math equations to control order of operations |
    147 | 3 | Function Calls | function(Var) | Calls said function with given Var |
    148 | 4 | Method Calls | Var:method(...) | calls the method() function on the given Var |
    149 | 4 | Indexing | Var[Value,type] | Will attempt to locate the provided Value with the provided type within the provided Var |
    150 | 5 | Unary plus | +Var | Returns the identity (same value) of Var |
    151 | 5 | Unary minus | -Var | Negates the value of Var |
    152 | 5 | Logical NOT | !Var | if something returns true, attaching this operator will make it return false |
    153 | 6 | Exponentiation | A ^ B | Raised A to the power of B |
    154 | 7 | Multiplication | A * B | Multiplies A by B |
    155 | 7 | Division | A / B | Divides A by B |
    156 | 7 | Modulo | A % B | Returns the remainder of division |
    157 | 8 | Addition | A + B | Adds A and B |
    158 | 8 | Subtraction | A - B | Subtracts A and B |
    159 | 9 | Binary Left Shift | A << B | Equivalent to A * (2^B) |
    160 | 9 | Binary Right Shift | A >> B | Equivalent to floor(A/(2^B)) |
    161 | 10 | Greater Than | A > B | if A's value is more than B |
    162 | 10 | Less Than | A < B | if A's value is less than B |
    163 | 10 | Greater Than or Equal to | A >= B | if A's value is more than or equal to B |
    164 | 10 | Less Than or Equal to | A <= B | if A's value is less than or equal to B |
    165 | 11 | Equals | A == B | if A's value equals B's value |
    166 | 11 | NOT Equals | A != B | if A doesn't equal the value of B |
    167 | 12 | Binary XOR | A ^^ B | Returns the binary XOR of A and B. |
    168 | 13 | Binary AND | A && B | Note that this is reversed with the "classical" & operator |
    169 | 14 | Binary OR | A \|\| B | Note that this is reversed with the "classical" \| operator |
    170 | 15 | Logical AND | A & B | Note that this is reversed with the "classical" && operator |
    171 | 16 | Logical OR | A \| B | Note that this is reversed with the "classical" \|\| operator |
    172 | 17 | Ternary Conditional | A ? B : C | Evaluates to B if A is truthy, otherwise C |
    173 | 17 | Binary Conditional | A ?: B | Equivalent to A ? A : B |
    174 | 18 | Assignment | A = B | The value of A now equals the value of B |
    175 It's important to note that some operators work with other types, such as vector arithmetic with +, -, *, and / (per-component), and string concatenation with + (although format or concat should be used for most concatenation operations).
    176 Scopes & Conditionals
    177 Scopes restrict variables to a particular code block (usually enclosed by curly braces { <CODE HERE> }). The highest level of scope outside of any blocks is called the "global" scope, where @persist, @inputs, and @outputs variables are stored, allowing them to be accessed from anywhere in the code.
    178 > [!Important]
    179 > E2 does not use typical booleans, and instead uses *truthiness* (or [*truth value*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Truth_value#Computing)). In place of booleans, most E2 expressions use 0 to represent *falsiness* and 1 or non-zero to represent *truthiness*.
    180 >
    181 > However, you're not limited to using numbers. Every built-in type in E2 has a truth value test to it, which determines an object's truthiness. For example, the string "" is falsy while "0" is truthy. Empty arrays and tables are falsy while filled ones are truthy.
    182 >
    183 > Generally, you can expect that for any type, it's falsy value is its default, uninitialized value, also called a *zero* value.
    184 if
    185 An if statement executes a block of code only if a condition is met (i.e., the passed variable is non-zero).
    186 <start codeblock>
    187 if (1) {
    188 print("This will run")
    189 }
    190 <end codeblock>
    191 elseif
    192 By using elseif, you can chain conditions together.
    193 <start codeblock>
    194 if (0) {
    195 print("never runs since 0 does not meet condition")
    196 } elseif (2) {
    197 print("This will run since the first if statement failed AND this if statement passes ")
    198 }
    199 <end codeblock>
    200 else
    201 else is used to handle cases where none of the conditions are met.
    202 <start codeblock>
    203 if (0) {
    204 print("This will not run since (0) is not truthy")
    205 } else {
    206 print("This will always run")
    207 }
    208 <end codeblock>
    209 Switch Statements
    210 A switch statement is similar to an if chain and allows for "fallthrough" behavior. If you omit the break statement after each case, it will execute every case underneath it (even if the condition isn't met) until it finds a break or reaches the end of the switch block.
    211 > [!NOTE]
    212 > For performance reasons, you should avoid using switch statements when possible.
    213 <start codeblock>
    214 switch (Var) {
    215 case 2,
    216 print("Var is 2")
    217 break
    218 case 3,
    219 print("Var is 3")
    220 break
    221 case 4,
    222 print("Var is 4") # Will fall through to the default case as well
    223 default,
    224 print("Var is not 2 or 3")
    225 }
    226 <end codeblock>
    227 <details>
    228 <summary>Equivalent code using if statements</summary>
    229 <start codeblock>
    230 if(Var == 2) {
    231 print("Var is 2")
    232 } elseif(Var == 3) {
    233 print("Var is 3")
    234 } else {
    235 if(Var == 4) {
    236 print("Var is 4")
    237 }
    238 print("Var is not 2 or 3")
    239 }
    240 <end codeblock>
    241 </details>
    242 Loops
    243 for
    244 The for loop consists of three numbers: the first represents the current iteration count, the second represents the iteration count at which the loop should end, and the optional third number represents the optional increment *step* value at each iteration. By default, the *step* count is 1.
    245 <start codeblock>
    246 This will call the code 5 times (1 - 5 inclusive). In this case, the third argument is redundant.
    247 for (I = 1, 5, 1) {
    248 ...
    249 }
    250 <end codeblock>
    251 > [!NOTE]
    252 > If you don't need to keep track of the iteration count in a for loop, you can discard the iteration variable to save a bit of performance.
    253 while
    254 A while loop will execute the code within its block as long as the specified condition is true. It's important to note that while loops can be unstable without perf() included in the conditional statement.
    255 <start codeblock>
    256 while (perf(80)){
    257 ...
    258 }
    259 <end codeblock>
    260 do while
    261 A do while loop is similar to a while loop, but it will always execute its block of code at least once. It checks the condition at the end of each iteration to determine whether to continue or exit the loop.
    262 <end codeblock>ts
    263 do {
    264 ...
    265 } while (perf(80))
    266 <end codeblock>
    267 foreach
    268 The foreach loop allows you to iterate through all the values of an array or table.
    269 <end codeblock>csharp
    270 foreach(Key:number, Value:entity = findToArray()) {
    271 ...
    272 }
    273 <end codeblock>
    274 It's recommended to annotate the type of keys when iterating through a table using foreach. By default, foreach on a table will iterate through string keys. To iterate through number keys, annotate with :number.
    275 <end codeblock>csharp
    276 foreach(Key:string, Value:number = MyTable) {}
    277 <end codeblock>
    278 break
    279 The break keyword allows you to exit a loop prematurely.
    280 <start codeblock>
    281 foreach(K, Ply:entity = players()) {
    282 if (Ply:distance(entity()) < 400) {
    283 break
    284 }
    285 Haven't found a player closer than 400 units yet
    286 }
    287 <end codeblock>
    288 continue
    289 The continue keyword allows you to skip a single iteration of a loop.
    290 <end codeblock>ts
    291 for (I = 1, 5) {
    292 if (I % 2 == 0) {
    293 continue  # Skip even numbers (You should use the for loop step parameter instead, though).
    294 }
    295 }
    296 <end codeblock>
    297 User Defined Functions
    298 Functions help to improve code organization and readability by allowing you to break down code into reusable and modular components.
    299 Basic Functions
    300 A function can be defined using the following syntax:
    301 <end codeblock>js
    302 function helloWorld() {
    303 print("Hello world!")
    304 }
    305 helloWorld()
    306 <end codeblock>
    307 This function will have a return type of void, which means that it does not output a value.
    308 Function Parameters
    309 > [!NOTE]
    310 > Function parameters are assumed to be numbers by default, unless you specify a different data type using the format <NAME>:<TYPE>.
    311 > This behavior shouldn't be relied on and is deprecated, though.
    312 <end codeblock>js
    313 function hello(Text:string) {
    314 print("Hello ", Text)
    315 }
    316 hello("World!")
    317 <end codeblock>
    318 Function Returns
    319 You can specify the return type of a function to let you pass values from it to another piece of code.
    320 <end codeblock>ts
    321 function string compliment(Name:string) {
    322 return "You look nice, " + Name + "!"
    323 }
    324 print(compliment(owner():name()))
    325 <end codeblock>
    326 > [!IMPORTANT]
    327 > You are required to make sure your function returns at the end of all code paths. The editor will error if you do not. If you're not sure where to place the return, put it at the very end of your function.
    328 Variadic Parameters
    329 Variadic parameters allow you to call a function with a varying amount of parameters.
    330 This is essentially just a function that takes an array, but it allows you to pass the arguments to the function directly rather than needing to wrap the arguments in an array()
    331 <start codeblock>
    332 This function calls printColor with a prefix [neat] .
    333 function printMessage(...Args:array) {
    334 	printColor(  array(vec(0, 172, 0), "[neat] ", vec(255)):add(Args) )
    335 }
    336 printMessage("Cool! Here's a number: ", randint(1, 27), ".")
    337 <end codeblock>
    338 You can also define the variadic parameter as a table, which allows you to use arrays and tables in the function call.
    339 <start codeblock>
    340 Sums all arrays together
    341 function number arraySum(...Args:table) {
    342 local Sum = 0
    343 foreach(_:number, R:array = Args) {
    344 Sum += R:sum()
    345 }
    346 return Sum
    347 }
    348 print(arraySum(array(6, 1), array(11))) # Prints "18"
    349 <end codeblock>
    350 User-Defined Methods
    351 (Formerly called meta-functions)
    352 A method is prefixed by a type followed by a colon. This is functionally identical to a normal function, but looks nicer.
    353 <start codeblock>
    354 function entity:hello() {
    355 print("Hello " + This:name())
    356 }
    357 owner():hello() # Prints "Hello " followed by your username
    358 <end codeblock>
    359 Lambda Functions
    360 Lambdas are functions that can be stored in variables, also known as [first-class functions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First-class_function). For simplicity, you should use [normal functions](#basic-functions) when you don't need the flexibility of lambdas.
    361 Lambdas are quite simple to use. Its syntax is similar to creating a function, and you call a lambda similarly to a normal function.
    362 <start codeblock>
    363 let MyLambda = function(S:string) {
    364 print(S)
    365 }
    366 MyLambda("Hello, World!") # Prints "Hello, World!"
    367 <end codeblock>
    368 Lambdas automatically determine their return type when you define them. To retrieve the value of a lambda return, you'll need to specify the return type in [brackets] after the lambda call.
    369 <start codeblock>
    370 let Runs = 0
    371 let GetRun = function() {
    372 Runs++
    373 return Runs
    374 }
    375 print(GetRun()[number])
    376 print(GetRun()) # ERROR! GetRun is assumed to return void here
    377 <end codeblock>
    378 Lambdas work just like any other type, so you can pass them to functions and return them. You can also define a lambda without storing them and pass them directly (known as a *function literal*).
    379 <start codeblock>
    380 let Wrapper = function(Func:function) {
    381 return function() { # Create and return function literal
    382 print("Wrapped!")
    383 Func()
    384 }
    385 }
    386 let Wrapped = Wrapper(function() { # Create and pass a function literal
    387 print("Hello, World!")
    388 })[function]
    389 Wrapped() # Prints "Wrapped!" and "Hello, World!"
    390 <end codeblock>
    391 *See also: [E2 Guide: Lambdas](/wiremod/wire/wiki/E2-Guide:-Lambdas)*
    392 Calling functions with strings
    393 > [!WARNING]
    394 > String calling is deprecated and will not be supported in the future. Look above to [Lambda Functions](#lambda-functions) to use the replacement.
    395 Using string calls to dynamically call functions should be avoided due to their performance cost and hacky nature. ~~However, this can serve as a substitute for "delegates" or "lambdas" from other languages until they are available.~~
    396 <start codeblock>
    397 let F = "print"
    398 F("Hello world!") # Same as print("Hello world!")
    399 let X = "health"
    400 let OwnerHealth = X(owner())[number] # Same as owner():health()
    401 <end codeblock>
    402 > [!WARNING]
    403 > These are deprecated and have been superceded by lambdas.
    404 > Using them will error on @strict in the future.
    405 Specialized functions \(misc\)
    406 include
    407 The #include syntax in E2 is similar to that of C and C++. When an #include statement is encountered, E2 will execute the code in the specified file. It's recommended to put the #include statement inside an if(first()) statement, and note that despite its appearance, it is parsed like a normal statement and is not related to the preprocessor.
    408 <start codeblock>
    409 example_lib.txt
    410 function doStuff() {
    411 print("Hello world!")
    412 }
    413 <end codeblock>
    414 <start codeblock>
    415 if (first()) {
    416 include "example_lib"
    417 ^^ make sure not to include .txt ^^
    418 Now you can use functions and global variables from the "example_lib" file.
    419 doStuff()
    420 }
    421 <end codeblock>
    422 Exception Handling
    423 By default, Expression 2 does not often throw errors; instead, it will silently fail and return a default value on function calls. However, if you enable the @strict directive, these errors will be thrown as proper runtime errors. To handle them, you should use try and catch blocks.
    424 <start codeblock>
    425 try { # < -- If an error occurs in this block, it will exit the block and call the catch {} block, passing the error message string.
    426 error("Unexpected error")
    427 } catch(E:string) { # < -- Can rename E to anything. It just stores the error message.
    428 assert(E == "Unexpected error")
    429 }
    430 <end codeblock>
    431 However, it's important to note that this only covers errors that occur within Expression 2 and not internal Lua errors caused by E2 extensions.
    432 Events
    433 *Main article: [Expression 2 Events](/wiremod/wire/wiki/Expression-2-Events)*
    434 Expression 2 inherited a problematic "clk" system from E1, which involved re-running the code and checking a variable to determine what caused it to run, leading to confusion and headaches. To address this issue, the event system was created as a replacement.
    435 <start codeblock>
    436 event chat(Ply:entity, Said:string, Team:number) {
    437 print(Ply, " just said ", Said)
    438 }
    439 Owner = owner()
    440 event keyPressed(Ply:entity, Key:string, Down:number, Bind:string) {
    441 if (Ply == Owner & !Down) {
    442 print("Owner released key " + Key)
    443 }
    444 }
    445 <end codeblock>
    446 See all events on the [Expression2 Events](/wiremod/wire/wiki/Expression-2-Events) page.
    447 ---

Name: Prop-core

    0 Description
    1 The prop core functionality is used generally for manipulating props using an E2 script within the Garry's Mod environment. Manipulation type can be anything like creating, deleting, teleporting, angling, gravity, inertia, buoyancy and much more. The data types are general for the Expression 2 chip and you can find them elsewhere.
    2 
    3 What convars can be used to setup it
    4 
    5 sbox_E2_maxProps          : Controls the maximum amount of props spawned via E2 set this to -1 to disable the limit.
    6 sbox_E2_maxPropsPerSecond : Controls the maximum amount of props spawned for one second. Don't set this too high!
    7 sbox_E2_PropCore          : Controls enable/disable of the extension. Setup values are written below.
    8 0 : The extension is disabled.
    9 1 : Only admins can use the extension.
    10 2 : Players can affect their own props.
    11 
    12 Expression 2 API
    13 All the function descriptions are available in the table below:
    14          Instance creator         | Out | Description 
    15 :---------------------------------|:---:|:------------
    16 propSpawn(EntityType,VectorType,NumberType)|EntityType|Rotation, Frozen Spawns a prop with the model of the template entity and rotated to the angle given. If frozen is 0, then it will spawn unfrozen.
    17 propSpawn(EntityType,NumberType)|EntityType|Entity template, Frozen Spawns a prop with the model of the template entity. If frozen is 0, then it will spawn unfrozen.
    18 propSpawn(EntityType,Vector2Type,VectorType,NumberType)|EntityType|Position, Rotation, Frozen Spawns a prop with the model of the template entity, at the position denoted by the vector, and rotated to the angle given. If frozen is 0, then it will spawn unfrozen.
    19 propSpawn(EntityType,Vector2Type,NumberType)|EntityType|Entity template, Position, Frozen Spawns a prop with the model of the template entity at the position denoted by the vector. If frozen is 0, then it will spawn unfrozen.
    20 propSpawn(StringType,VectorType,NumberType)|EntityType|Model path, Rotation, Frozen Spawns a prop with the model denoted by the string filepath and rotated to the angle given. If frozen is 0, then it will spawn unfrozen.
    21 propSpawn(StringType,NumberType)|EntityType|Use the model string or a template entity to spawn a prop. You can set the position and/or the rotation as well. The last number indicates frozen/unfrozen.
    22 propSpawn(StringType,Vector2Type,VectorType,NumberType)|EntityType|Model path, Position, Rotation, Frozen Spawns a prop with the model denoted by the string file path, at the position denoted by the vector, and rotated to the angle given. If frozen is 0, then it will spawn unfrozen.
    23 propSpawn(StringType,Vector2Type,NumberType)|EntityType|Model path, Position, Frozen Spawns a prop with the model denoted by the string filepath at the position denoted by the vector. If frozen is 0, then it will spawn unfrozen.
    24 seatSpawn(StringType,NumberType)|EntityType|Model path, Frozen Spawns a prop with the model denoted by the string filepath. If frozen is 0, then it will spawn unfrozen.
    25 seatSpawn(StringType,Vector2Type,VectorType,NumberType)|EntityType|Model path, Frozen Spawns a prop with the model denoted by the string filepath. If frozen is 0, then it will spawn unfrozen.
    26                Prop core method               | Out | Description 
    27 :---------------------------------------------|:---:|:------------
    28 EntityType:deparent() Unparents an entity, so it moves freely again.
    29 EntityType:parentTo() Parents one entity to another.
    30 EntityType:parentTo(EntityType) Parents one entity to another.
    31 EntityType:propBreak() Breaks/Explodes breakable/explodable props (Useful for Mines).
    32 EntityType:propDelete() Deletes the specified prop.
    33 EntityType:propDrag(NumberType) Passing 0 makes the entity not be affected by drag
    34 EntityType:propDraw(NumberType) Passing 0 disables rendering for the entity (makes it really invisible)
    35 EntityType:propFreeze(NumberType) Passing 0 unfreezes the entity, everything else freezes it.
    36 EntityType:propGetElasticity()|NumberType|Gets prop's elasticity coefficient
    37 EntityType:propGetFriction()|NumberType|Gets prop's friction coefficient
    38 EntityType:propGravity(NumberType) Passing 0 makes the entity weightless, everything else makes it weighty.
    39 EntityType:propInertia(Vector2Type) Sets the directional inertia
    40 EntityType:propMakePersistent(NumberType) Setting to 1 will make the prop persistent.
    41 EntityType:propManipulate(Vector2Type,VectorType,NumberType,NumberType,NumberType) Allows to do any single prop core function in one term (position, rotation, freeze, gravity, notsolid)
    42 EntityType:propNotSolid(NumberType) Passing 0 makes the entity solid, everything else makes it non-solid.
    43 EntityType:propPhysicalMaterial()|StringType|Returns the surface material of a prop.
    44 EntityType:propPhysicalMaterial(StringType) Changes the surface material of a prop (eg. wood, metal, ... See [Material_surface_properties](https://developer.valvesoftware.com/wiki/Material_surface_properties) ).
    45 EntityType:propSetBuoyancy(NumberType) Sets the prop's buoyancy ratio from 0 to 1
    46 EntityType:propSetElasticity(NumberType) Sets prop's elasticity coefficient (default is 1)
    47 EntityType:propSetFriction(NumberType) Sets prop's friction coefficient (default is 1)
    48 EntityType:propSetVelocity(Vector2Type) Sets the velocity of the prop for the next iteration
    49 EntityType:propSetVelocityInstant(Vector2Type) Sets the initial velocity of the prop
    50 EntityType:propShadow(NumberType) Passing 0 disables rendering for the entity's shadow
    51 EntityType:propStatic(NumberType) Sets to 1 to make the entity static (disables movement, physgun, unfreeze, drive...) or 0 to cancel.
    52 EntityType:reposition(Vector2Type) Deprecated. Kept for backwards-compatibility.
    53 EntityType:rerotate(VectorType) Deprecated. Kept for backwards-compatibility.
    54 EntityType:setAng(VectorType) Set the rotation of an entity.
    55 EntityType:setPos(Vector2Type) Sets the position of an entity.
    56 EntityType:use() Simulates a player pressing their use key on the entity.
    57         General functions         | Out | Description 
    58 :---------------------------------|:---:|:------------
    59 propCanCreate()|NumberType|Returns 1 when propSpawn() will successfully spawn a prop until the limit is reached.
    60 ArrayType:propDelete()|NumberType|Deletes all the props in the given array, returns the amount of props deleted.
    61 TableType:propDelete()|NumberType|Deletes all the props in the given table, returns the amount of props deleted.
    62 propDeleteAll() Removes all entities spawned by this E2
    63 propSpawnEffect(NumberType) Set to 1 to enable prop spawn effect, 0 to disable.
    64 propSpawnUndo(NumberType) Set to 0 to force prop removal on E2 shutdown, and suppress Undo entries for props.

Name: wire-about
Index: 65
MIME: text/plain
Size (bytes): 392
Lines: 2
Path: /home/ryan/.local/share/Steam/steamapps/common/GarrysMod/garrysmod/data/expression2/rag/textdocs/v1/wire-about.md
    0 What is Wiremod?
    1 Wiremod is an addon that was created by Erkle, and is now maintained by the Wire Team. This addon allows the user to spawn gates, sensors, inputs and outputs and wire them together into working, computer-like contraptions in Garry's Mod. The gates are connected with wires, which are beams that act as a medium to carry the output from one wired entity to an input on another.
